<p><i><b>Babylon 5</b></i> is an American <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> television series created by writer and producer <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Straczynski" title="J. Michael Straczynski">J. Michael Straczynski</a>, under the Babylonian Productions label, in association with Straczynski's Synthetic Worlds Ltd. and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Television" title="Warner Bros. Television">Warner Bros. Domestic Television</a>. After the successful airing of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Test_pilot_movie" title="Test pilot movie">test pilot movie</a> on February 22, 1993, <i><a href="/wiki/Babylon_5:_The_Gathering" title="Babylon 5: The Gathering">Babylon 5: The Gathering</a></i>, in May 1993 Warner Brothers commissioned the series for production as part of its <a href="/wiki/Prime_Time_Entertainment_Network" title="Prime Time Entertainment Network">Prime Time Entertainment Network</a> (PTEN).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first season premiered in the US on January 26, 1994, and the series ultimately ran for the intended five seasons. Describing it as having "always been conceived as, fundamentally, a five year story, a novel for television", Straczynski wrote 92 of the 110 episodes, and served as executive producer, along with <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Netter" title="Douglas Netter">Douglas Netter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting">Setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Set between the years 2257 and 2262, it depicts a future where Earth has sovereign states, and a unifying <a href="/wiki/Earth_Alliance_(Babylon_5)#Early_development" title="Earth Alliance (Babylon 5)">Earth government</a>. Colonies within the solar system, and beyond, make up the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Alliance_(Babylon_5)" title="Earth Alliance (Babylon 5)">Earth Alliance</a>, and contact has been made with other <a href="/wiki/Spacefaring#Spacefaring_in_popular_culture" title="Spacefaring">spacefaring</a> species. The <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a> portray alien ambassadorial staff and humans assigned to the 5-mile (8.0 km)-long <a href="/wiki/Babylon_5_(space_station)" title="Babylon 5 (space station)"><i>Babylon 5</i> space station</a>, a center for trade and diplomacy. Described as "one of the most complex programs on television",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4thSeason_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-4thSeason-3">[3]</a></sup> the various <a href="/wiki/Story_arc" title="Story arc">story arcs</a> drew upon the prophesies, religious zealotry, racial tensions, social pressures, and political rivalries which existed within each of their cultures, to create a contextual framework for the motivations and consequences of the protagonists' actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4thSeason_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-4thSeason-3">[3]</a></sup> With a strong emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Characterization#Character_development" title="Characterization">character development</a> set against a backdrop of conflicting ideologies on multiple levels, Straczynski wanted "to take an adult approach to <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">SF</a>, and attempt to do for television SF what <i><a href="/wiki/Hill_Street_Blues" title="Hill Street Blues">Hill Street Blues</a></i> did for cop shows."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Generally viewed as having "launched the new era of television CGI visual effects",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> it received multiple awards during its initial run, including two consecutive Hugo Awards for <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation" title="Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation">best dramatic presentation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugo1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hugo1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugo2_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hugo2-7">[7]</a></sup> and continues to regularly feature prominently in various polls and listings highlighting top-rated science fiction series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Not appearing on American television since 2003, it continues to be shown in international markets such as <a href="/wiki/Fox_(UK_and_Ireland)" title="Fox (UK and Ireland)">Fox</a> in the UK, the <a href="/wiki/TV4_Science_fiction" title="TV4 Science fiction">TV4-ScifFi</a> Channel in Sweden, and the <a href="/wiki/FBC_TV" title="FBC TV">FBC TV</a> channel in Fiji.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Initially written by Straczynski, <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC</a> began publishing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylon_5_novels,_short_stories_and_comic_books#Comic_books" title="Babylon 5 novels, short stories and comic books">Babylon 5 comics</a> in 1994, with stories that closely tied in with events depicted in the show, with events in the comics eventually being referenced onscreen in the actual television series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Media_franchise#Development_to_other_forms" title="Media franchise">franchise</a> continued to expand into short stories, RPG's, and novels, with the <a href="/wiki/Technomage#In_books" title="Technomage">Technomage trilogy</a> of books being the last to be published in 2001, shortly after the spin-off television series, <i><a href="/wiki/Crusade_(TV_series)" title="Crusade (TV series)">Crusade</a></i>, was cancelled. Excepting movie rights, which are retained by Straczynski, all production rights for the franchise are owned by Warner Bros.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot_summary">Plot summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Plot summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Backstory">Backstory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Backstory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Civilizations_in_Babylon_5" title="Civilizations in Babylon 5">Civilizations in Babylon 5</a></div>
<p>At the beginning of the series, five dominant civilizations (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_(Babylon_5)" title="Human (Babylon 5)">Humans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minbari" title="Minbari">Minbari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narn" title="Narn">Narn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centauri_(Babylon_5)" title="Centauri (Babylon 5)">Centauri</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vorlon" title="Vorlon">Vorlons</a>) are presented. "The <a href="/wiki/Shadow_(Babylon_5)" title="Shadow (Babylon 5)">Shadows</a>" and their various allies are malevolent species who appear later in the series. Several dozen less powerful species from the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Non-Aligned_Worlds" title="League of Non-Aligned Worlds">League of Non-Aligned Worlds</a> appear, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drazi" title="Drazi">Drazi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brakiri" title="Brakiri">Brakiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vree" title="Vree">Vree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civilizations_in_Babylon_5#Markab" title="Civilizations in Babylon 5">Markab</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pak%27ma%27ra" title="Pak'ma'ra">pak'ma'ra</a>. The station's first three predecessors (the original <i>Babylon</i> station, <i>Babylon 2</i> and <i>Babylon 3</i>) were sabotaged or accidentally destroyed before their completion. The fourth station, <i><a href="/wiki/Babylon_4" title="Babylon 4">Babylon 4</a></i>, vanished without a trace twenty-four hours after it became fully operational.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-january_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-january-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>The television series takes its name from the <a href="/wiki/Babylon_5_(space_station)" title="Babylon 5 (space station)"><i>Babylon 5</i> space station</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_Eridani" title="Epsilon Eridani">Epsilon Eridani</a> star system, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trojan_points" title="Trojan points">fifth Lagrangian point</a> between the fictional planet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epsilon_III" title="Epsilon III">Epsilon III</a> and its moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <i>Babylon 5</i> is an <a href="/wiki/O%27Neill_cylinder" title="O'Neill cylinder">O'Neill cylinder</a> five miles long and a half-mile to a mile in diameter. Living areas accommodate the various alien species, providing differing atmospheres and gravities. Human visitors to the alien sectors are shown using breathing equipment and other measures to tolerate the conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The five seasons of the series each correspond to one fictional sequential year in the period 2258–2262. Each season shares its name with an episode that is central to that season's plot. As the series starts, the <i>Babylon 5</i> station is welcoming ambassadors from various races in the galaxy. Earth has just barely survived an accidental war with the much more powerful <a href="/wiki/Minbari" title="Minbari">Minbari</a>, who, despite their superior technology, mysteriously surrendered at the brink of the destruction of the human race during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Line" title="Battle of the Line">Battle of the Line</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1_.E2.80.93_Year_2258">Season 1 – Year 2258</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Season 1 – Year 2258">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_episodes#Season_1:_Signs_and_Portents" title="List of Babylon 5 episodes">List of Babylon 5 episodes § Season 1: Signs and Portents</a></div>
<p>During 2258, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sinclair" title="Jeffrey Sinclair">Commander Jeffrey Sinclair</a> is in charge of the station. Much of the story revolves around his gradual discovery that it was his capture by the Minbari at the Battle of the Line which ended the war against Earth. Upon capturing Sinclair, the Minbari came to believe that he was the reincarnation of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_characters#V" title="List of Babylon 5 characters">Valen</a>, a great Minbari leader and hero of the last Minbari-Shadow war. Inferring that others of their species had been and were continuing to be reborn as humans, and in obedience to the edict that Minbari do not kill one another lest they harm the soul, they stopped the war just as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth_(Babylon_5)" title="Earth (Babylon 5)">Earth's</a> final defenses were on the verge of collapse.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, tensions between the Centauri Republic, which is an empire in decline, and the Narn Regime, a former dominion which rebelled and gained freedom, are increasing. Ambassador G'Kar of the Narn wishes for his people to strike back at the Centauri for what they did, and Ambassador Londo Mollari of the Centauri wishes for his people to become again the great empire they once were. As part of these struggles, Mollari makes a deal with a mysterious ally to strike back at the Narn, further heightening tensions.</p>
<p>It is gradually revealed that <a href="/wiki/Delenn" title="Delenn">Ambassador Delenn</a> is a member of the mysterious and powerful <a href="/wiki/Grey_Council" title="Grey Council">Grey Council</a>, the ruling body of the Minbari. Towards the end of 2258, she begins the transformation into a Minbari-human hybrid, ostensibly to build a bridge between the humans and Minbari. The year ends with the death of <a href="/wiki/Earth_Alliance_(Babylon_5)" title="Earth Alliance (Babylon 5)">Earth Alliance</a> president Luis Santiago. The death is officially ruled an accident, but some members of the military, including the staff of <i>Babylon 5</i>, believe it to be an assassination.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2_.E2.80.93_Year_2259">Season 2 – Year 2259</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Season 2 – Year 2259">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_episodes#Season_2:_The_Coming_of_Shadows" title="List of Babylon 5 episodes">List of Babylon 5 episodes § Season 2: The Coming of Shadows</a></div>
<p>At the beginning of 2259, <a href="/wiki/John_Sheridan_(Babylon_5)" title="John Sheridan (Babylon 5)">Captain John Sheridan</a> replaces Sinclair as the military governor of the station after Sinclair is reassigned as ambassador to Minbar. He and the command staff gradually learn that the assassination of President Santiago was arranged by his then-Vice President, Morgan Clark, who has now become president. Conflict develops between the <i>Babylon 5</i> command staff and the <a href="/wiki/Psi_Corps" title="Psi Corps">Psi Corps</a>, an increasingly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocratic" title="Autocratic">autocratic</a> organization which oversees and controls the lives of human <a href="/wiki/Telepathy" title="Telepathy">telepaths</a>.</p>
<p>The Shadows, an ancient and extremely powerful race who have recently emerged from hibernation, are revealed to be the cause of a variety of mysterious and disturbing events, including the attack on the Narn outpost at the end of 2258. Centauri Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Londo_Mollari" title="Londo Mollari">Londo Mollari</a> unknowingly enlists their aid through his association with their mysterious human representative <a href="/wiki/Morden_(Babylon_5)" title="Morden (Babylon 5)">Mr. Morden</a> in the ongoing conflict with the Narn. The elderly and ailing Centauri emperor, long an advocate of reconciliation with the Narn, unfortunately has insufficient control to prevent others from instigating war against the Narn Regime. When the emperor dies suddenly during a peace mission to <i>Babylon 5</i>, a number of conspirators, including Ambassador Londo Mollari and Lord Refa, take control of the Centauri government by assassinating their opponents and placing the late emperor's unstable nephew on the throne. Their first act is to start open aggression against the Narn. After a full-scale war breaks out, the Centauri with the help of the Shadows through Londo eventually conquer Narn in a brutal attack involving <a href="/wiki/List_of_electromagnetic_projectile_devices_in_fiction" title="List of electromagnetic projectile devices in fiction">mass drivers</a>, outlawed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a>. Towards the end of the year, the Clark administration begins to show increasingly totalitarian characteristics, clamping down on dissent and restricting <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Vorlon" title="Vorlon">Vorlons</a> are revealed to be the basis of legends about <a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angels</a> on various worlds, including Earth, and are the ancient enemies of the Shadows. They enlist the aid of Sheridan and the <i>Babylon 5</i> command staff in the struggle against the Shadows.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_3_.E2.80.93_Year_2260">Season 3 – Year 2260</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Season 3 – Year 2260">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_episodes#Season_3:_Point_of_No_Return" title="List of Babylon 5 episodes">List of Babylon 5 episodes § Season 3: Point of No Return</a></div>
<p>The Psi Corps and President Clark, whose government has discovered Shadow vessels buried in Earth's solar system, begin to harness the vessels' advanced technology. The Clark administration continues to become increasingly <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobic</a> and totalitarian, and gradually develops an <a href="/wiki/Orwellian" title="Orwellian">Orwellian</a> government style, including an organization called Night Watch which targets citizens who hold views contrary to those of Clark's regime.</p>
<p>Sheridan and Delenn's "conspiracy of light" works to uncover clues about how to defeat the Shadows. During a mission near <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">Ganymede</a>, one of the moons of Jupiter, their ship is seen by the Earth Alliance destroyer <i>Agamemnon</i>, but not recognized. Though they escape and no shots were fired in the encounter, President Clark uses it as an excuse to declare martial law. This triggers a war of independence on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, which had long had a strained political relationship with Earth. <i>Babylon 5</i> attempts to avoid conflict with Earth, but in response to civilian bombings on Mars, concerns with Night Watch, and illegal orders meant to oppress their populations, they choose to declare independence from Earth, along with several other outlying Earth Alliance colonies including Orion VII and Proxima III. In response, the Earth Alliance attempts to retake <i>Babylon 5</i> by force, but with the aid of the Minbari, who have allied with the station against the growing Shadow threat, the attack is repelled at great cost.</p>
<p>Becoming concerned over the Shadows' growing influence among his people, Centauri ambassador Londo Mollari attempts to sever ties with them. <a href="/wiki/Morden_(Babylon_5)" title="Morden (Babylon 5)">Mr. Morden</a>, the Shadows' human representative, tricks him into restoring the partnership by engineering the murder of Mollari's mistress while putting the blame on a rival Centauri House. Open warfare breaks out between the Shadows and the alliance led by <i>Babylon 5</i> and the Minbari. It is learned that genetic manipulation by the Vorlons is the source of telepathy in humans and other races, as it is later discovered that Shadow ships are vulnerable to telepathic attacks. Displeased at the Vorlons' lack of direct action against the Shadows, Captain John Sheridan browbeats Vorlon ambassador <a href="/wiki/Kosh_Naranek" title="Kosh Naranek">Kosh Naranek</a> into launching an attack against their mutual enemy. Kosh's deeds lead to his subsequent assassination by the Shadows.</p>
<p>Former station commander Jeffrey Sinclair returns to <i>Babylon 5</i> to enlist the aid of Captain Sheridan, Delenn, Ivanova and Marcus in stealing the <i><a href="/wiki/Babylon_4" title="Babylon 4">Babylon 4</a></i> space station and sending it 1,000 years back in time to use it as a base of operations against the Shadows in the previous Minbari-Shadow war. Having undergone a similar transformation to the one Delenn had at the end of Season 1, Sinclair transforms into a Minbari and is subsequently revealed to be the actual Valen of Minbari legend, rather than simply a reincarnation. Meanwhile, as a result of the unstable time travel, Sheridan sees a vision of the downfall of Centauri Prime when it is attacked by Shadow allies after the Shadow war, and he becomes determined to prevent that future.</p>
<p>Sheridan and Delenn begin a romantic relationship, but their lives and the war are interrupted by the sudden reappearance of Sheridan's wife, who was presumed dead after taking part in an archaeological expedition to Z'ha'dum years prior. She tells Sheridan that the Shadows are not evil, hoping to bring him back with her and recruit him to their cause. He soon realizes that her mind has been tampered with and corrupted by the Shadows, but accepts her offer to visit Z'ha'dum because he hopes it will save the galaxy sooner and prevent the downfall of Centauri Prime. He takes with him a pair of nuclear warheads, which he uses to destroy their largest city, and is last seen jumping into a miles-deep pit to escape the explosion.</p>
<p>Shadow vessels appear at the station, but disappear after Sheridan's attack. However, after they leave, station personnel realize that Garibaldi, who left in a fighter to defend against the vessels, never returned.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_4_.E2.80.93_Year_2261">Season 4 – Year 2261</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Season 4 – Year 2261">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_episodes#Season_4:_No_Surrender.2C_No_Retreat" title="List of Babylon 5 episodes">List of Babylon 5 episodes § Season 4: No Surrender, No Retreat</a></div>
<p>In 2261, the Vorlons join the Shadow War, but their tactics become a concern for the alliance when the Vorlons begin destroying entire planets which they deem to have been "influenced" by the Shadows. Disturbed by this turn of events, Babylon 5 recruits several other powerful and ancient races (the <a href="/wiki/First_Ones" title="First Ones">First Ones</a>) to their cause, against both the Shadows and the Vorlons. Captain John Sheridan returns to the station after escaping from Z'ha'dum and reunites the galaxy against the Shadows, but at a price: barring illness or injury, he has only 20 years left to live. He is accompanied by a mysterious alien named Lorien who claims to be the first sentient being in the galaxy, and who breathed life into Sheridan at Z'ha'dum. Once Sheridan returns, he and Delenn formalize their relationship and begin planning to marry, although most of their plans are put on hold due to the ongoing war.</p>
<p>Hours before Sheridan's return, Garibaldi is rescued and returned to the station, in rather dubious circumstances. Over the course of the next several months, he becomes markedly more paranoid and suspicious of other alien races and of Sheridan than he was before, causing worry among his friends and colleagues.</p>
<p>Centauri Emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartagia" title="Cartagia">Cartagia</a> forges a relationship with the Shadows. With the reluctant help of his enemy G'Kar, Londo Mollari engineers the assassination of Cartagia and repudiates his agreement with the Shadows. In exchange for G'Kar's help, Londo frees the Narn from Centauri occupation. Londo afterwards kills Mr. Morden and destroys the Shadow vessels based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centauri_Prime" title="Centauri Prime">Centauri homeworld</a>, in a successful attempt to save his planet from destruction by the Vorlons. Aided by the other ancient races, and several younger ones, Sheridan lures both the Vorlons and the Shadows into an immense battle, during which the <a href="/wiki/Vorlon" title="Vorlon">Vorlons</a> and Shadows reveal that they have been left as guardians of the younger races, but due to philosophical differences, ended up using them as pawns in their endless <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a> throughout the ages. The younger races reject their continued interference, and the Vorlons and Shadows, along with the remaining First Ones, agree to depart the galaxy in order to allow the younger races to find their own way.</p>
<p>After the Shadows are defeated, Garibaldi leaves his post as security chief and works on his own as a "provider of information". He begins working for one William Edgars, a Mars tycoon, who is married to Garibaldi's former love. While he works ever closer with Edgars, he becomes increasingly aggressive toward Sheridan and eventually leaves <i>Babylon 5</i>.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minbar_(planet)" title="Minbar (planet)">Minbar</a> is gripped by a brief civil war between the Warrior and Religious castes. Delenn secretly meets with Neroon of the Warrior caste and convinces him that neither side can be allowed to win. She tells him that she will undergo a ritual wherein she will be willing to sacrifice herself, but will stop the ritual before she actually dies. When Neroon sees that she actually intends to go through the entire ritual, he rescues her and sacrifices himself instead, declaring that, although he was born Warrior caste, in his heart he is Religious caste.</p>
<p>As part of the ongoing conflict between Earth and Babylon 5, Garibaldi eventually betrays Sheridan and arranges his capture in order to gain Edgars' trust and learn his plans. Garibaldi later learns that Edgars had created a virus that is dangerous only to telepaths. It is then revealed that after Garibaldi was captured the previous year, he was taken to the Psi Corps and re-programmed by Bester to provide information to him at the right time. Bester releases Garibaldi of his programming, and allows him to remember everything he had done since being kidnapped. Edgars is killed by Psi Corps operatives. His wife disappears but is reunited with Garibaldi after the end of the war.</p>
<p>Sheridan is tortured and interrogated by those who hope to break him and turn him into a propaganda tool for Earth's totalitarian government. Fortunately, Garibaldi is able to help free Sheridan and return him to the campaign to free Earth. An alliance led by Babylon 5 frees Earth from totalitarian rule by president Clark in a short but bloody war. This culminates in Clark's suicide and the restoration of democratic government in the Earth Alliance. Mars is granted full independence, and Sheridan agrees to resign his commission. The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Non-Aligned_Worlds" title="League of Non-Aligned Worlds">League of Non-Aligned Worlds</a> is dissolved and reformed into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstellar_Alliance_(Babylon_5)" title="Interstellar Alliance (Babylon 5)">Interstellar Alliance</a>, with Sheridan elected as its first president and continuing his command of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anla%27shok" title="Anla'shok">Rangers</a>, who are to act as a galactic equivalent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeepers" title="United Nations peacekeepers">United Nations peacekeepers</a>. Londo and G'Kar enter an uneasy alliance to help both their races as well as Sheridan in forming the Interstellar Alliance. During the final battle to liberate Earth from Clark's regime, Ivanova is critically injured, promised only a few days to live. Marcus, who had fallen in love with Ivanova, finds the same alien healing device used to revive Garibaldi at the beginning of the second season, and uses it to transfer almost all of his life energy into Ivanova, causing her to live. This causes her immense emotional anguish, and she chooses to leave Babylon 5 for another posting in EarthForce. Marcus is placed into indefinite cryonic suspension at her request, pending resuscitation technology.</p>
<p>Sheridan and Delenn complete their marriage ceremony while en route to Babylon 5, where they will head the Interstellar Alliance until the completion of Alliance's permanent headquarters.</p>
<p>In the season finale, the events of 100, 500, 1000, and one million years into the future are shown, depicting Babylon 5's lasting influence throughout history. Among the events shown are the political aftermath of the 2261 civil war, a subsequent nuclear war on Earth involving a new totalitarian government in 2762, the resulting fall of Earth into a <a href="/wiki/Pre-industrial_society" title="Pre-industrial society">pre-industrial society</a>, the loss and restoration of humanity's knowledge of space travel, and the final evolution of mankind into energy beings similar to the Vorlons, after which Earth's sun goes <a href="/wiki/Nova" title="Nova">nova</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_5_.E2.80.93_Year_2262_and_beyond">Season 5 – Year 2262 and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Season 5 – Year 2262 and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Babylon_5_episodes#Season_5:_The_Wheel_of_Fire" title="List of Babylon 5 episodes">List of Babylon 5 episodes § Season 5: The Wheel of Fire</a></div>
<p>In 2262, Earthforce Captain <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Lochley" title="Elizabeth Lochley">Elizabeth Lochley</a> is appointed to command <i>Babylon 5</i>, which is now also the headquarters of the Interstellar Alliance. The station grows in its role as a sanctuary for rogue telepaths running from the <a href="/wiki/Psi_Corps" title="Psi Corps">Psi Corps</a>, resulting in conflict. <a href="/wiki/G%27Kar" title="G'Kar">G'Kar</a>, former Narn ambassador to <i>Babylon 5</i>, becomes unwillingly a spiritual icon after a book that he wrote while incarcerated during the Narn-Centauri War is published without his knowledge. The <a href="/wiki/Drakh" title="Drakh">Drakh</a>, former allies of the Shadows who remained in the galaxy, take control of <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">Regent</a> <a href="/wiki/Virini" title="Virini">Virini</a> on Centauri Prime through a parasitic creature called a Keeper, then incite a war between the Centauri and the Interstellar Alliance, in order to isolate the Centauri from the Alliance and gain a malleable homeworld for themselves.</p>
<p>Centauri Prime is devastated by <a href="/wiki/Narn" title="Narn">Narn</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drazi" title="Drazi">Drazi</a> warships and Londo Mollari becomes emperor, then ends the war. However, the Drakh blackmail him into accepting a Drakh Keeper, under threat of the complete nuclear destruction of the planet. <a href="/wiki/Vir_Cotto" title="Vir Cotto">Vir Cotto</a>, Mollari's loyal and more moral aide, becomes ambassador to <i>Babylon 5</i> in his stead. G'Kar also leaves <i>Babylon 5</i> to escape his unwanted fame and explore the rim. Sheridan and Delenn move to a city on Minbar, where the new headquarters of the Interstellar Alliance are located, while celebrating their first year of marriage and the upcoming birth of their son, and mourning the loss of dear friendships. Garibaldi marries and settles down on Mars, where he and his wife share ownership of a prominent pharmaceutical company. Most other main characters, including Stephen Franklin and Lyta Alexander, leave <i>Babylon 5</i> as well.</p>
<p>As shown in flash-forwards earlier in the series, the next several years include the reign of Londo Mollari as Centauri Emperor. Sixteen years later, Londo sacrifices his life to rescue Sheridan and Delenn from the Drakh, in the hope that they in turn can save Centauri Prime. To prevent the Drakh from discovering his ruse, he asks G'Kar, now an old friend, to kill him, but Londo's Keeper wakes up and forces him to kill G'Kar in return. They die at each other's throats, in accordance with Londo's vision many decades earlier, and Vir Cotto succeeds him as emperor, free of Drakh influence.</p>
<p>Three years after Londo's death, Sheridan himself is on the verge of death and takes one last opportunity to gather his old friends together. Shortly after his farewell party, Sheridan says goodbye to Delenn, though in Minbari fashion they use the word "goodnight" to signify their hope of an eventual reunion. Sheridan then takes a final trip to the obsolete <i>Babylon 5</i> station before its decommissioning. He returns to the site of the final battle between the Vorlons and the Shadows and apparently dies, but is instead claimed by The First One, who invites him to join the other First Ones on a journey beyond the rim of the galaxy. <i>Babylon 5</i> station is destroyed in a demolition shortly after Sheridan's departure, its existence no longer necessary as the Alliance has taken over its diplomatic purposes and other trading routes have been established. This final episode features a cameo by Straczynski as the technician who switches off the lights before <i>Babylon 5</i> is demolished.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Throughout its run, <i>Babylon 5</i> found ways to portray <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theme_(literature)" title="Theme (literature)">themes</a> relevant to modern and historical social issues. It marked several firsts in television science fiction, such as the exploration of the political and social landscapes of the first human colonies, their interactions with Earth, and the underlying tensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-mars-16">[16]</a></sup> <i>Babylon 5</i> was also one of the first television science fiction shows to <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/denotative" title="wikt:denotative">denotatively</a> refer to a <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_relationship" title="Same-sex relationship">same-sex relationship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dyke1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-dyke1-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dyke2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-dyke2-18">[18]</a></sup> In the show, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> is as much of an issue as "being left-handed or right-handed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jsgay1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-jsgay1-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unrequited_love" title="Unrequited love">Unrequited love</a> is explored as a source of pain for the characters, though not all the relationships end unhappily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soaps1_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-soaps1-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Order_vs._chaos.3B_authoritarianism_vs._free_will">Order vs. chaos; authoritarianism vs. free will</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Order vs. chaos; authoritarianism vs. free will">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:40%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>Neither the Vorlons nor the Shadows saw themselves as conquerors or adversaries. Both believed they were doing what was right for us. And like any possessive parent, they'll keep on believing that until the kid is strong enough to stand up and say, 'No, this is what <i><b>I</b></i> want.'</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—<a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Straczynski" title="J. Michael Straczynski">J. Michael Straczynski</a>, 1997<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-js_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-js-21">[21]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The clash between order and chaos, and the people caught in between, plays an important role in <i>Babylon 5</i>. The conflict between two unimaginably powerful older races, the <a href="/wiki/Vorlon" title="Vorlon">Vorlons</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shadow_(Babylon_5)" title="Shadow (Babylon 5)">Shadows</a>, is represented as a battle between two competing ideologies, each seeking to turn the humans and the other younger races to their beliefs. The Vorlons represent an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> philosophy: you will do what we tell you to, because we tell you to do it. The Vorlon question, "Who are you?" focuses on identity as a catalyst for shaping personal goals;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-signs_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-signs-23">[23]</a></sup> the intention is not to solicit a "correct" answer, but to "tear down the artifices we construct around ourselves until we're left facing ourselves, not our roles."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The Shadows represent another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> philosophy cloaked in a disguise of evolution through fire (as shown in the episode in which Sheridan goes to Z'ha'dum and when he refuses to cooperate, Justin tells him: "But we do what we're told... and so will you!"), of sowing the seeds of conflict in order to engender progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The question the Shadows ask is "What do you want?" In contrast to the Vorlons, they place personal desire and ambition first, using it to shape identity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-signs_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-signs-23">[23]</a></sup> encouraging conflict between groups who choose to serve their own glory or profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The representation of order and chaos was informed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonian_mythology" title="Babylonian mythology">Babylonian myth</a> that the universe was born in the conflict between both. The climax of this conflict comes with the younger races' exposing of the Vorlons' and the Shadows' "true faces"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-js_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-js-21">[21]</a></sup> and the rejection of both philosophies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-signs_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-signs-23">[23]</a></sup> heralding the dawn of a new age without their interference.</p>
<p>The notion that the war was about "killing your parents"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-js_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-js-21">[21]</a></sup> is echoed in the portrayal of the civil war between the human colonies and Earth. Deliberately dealing in historical and political metaphor, with particular emphasis upon <a href="/wiki/McCarthyism" title="McCarthyism">McCarthyism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_Un-American_Activities_Committee" title="House Un-American Activities Committee">HUAC</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commie_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-commie-27">[27]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Alliance_(Babylon_5)" title="Earth Alliance (Babylon 5)">Earth Alliance</a> becomes increasingly authoritarian, eventually sliding into a dictatorship. The show examines the impositions on <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a> under the pretext of greater defense against outside threats which aid its rise, and the self-delusion of a populace which believes its moral superiority will never allow a dictatorship to come to power, until it is too late.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The successful rebellion led by the Babylon 5 station results in the restoration of a democratic government, and true autonomy for Mars and the colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War_and_peace">War and peace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: War and peace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:40%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>What interests me, what I wanted to do with making this show, was in large measure to examine the issues and emotions and events that precede a war, precipitate a war, the effects of the war itself, the end of the war and the aftermath of the war. The war is hardware; the people are at the center of the story.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—J. Michael Straczynski, 1997<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jswar_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-jswar-30">[30]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The <i>Babylon 5</i> universe deals with numerous armed conflicts which range on an interstellar scale. The story begins in the aftermath of a war which brought the human race to the brink of extinction, caused by a misunderstanding during a <a href="/wiki/First_contact_(science_fiction)" title="First contact (science fiction)">first contact</a> situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-january_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-january-13">[13]</a></sup> The Babylon 5 station is subsequently built in order to foster peace through diplomacy, described as the "last, best hope for peace" in the opening credits monologue during its first three seasons. Wars between separate alien civilizations are featured. The conflict between the <a href="/wiki/Narn" title="Narn">Narn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Centauri_(Babylon_5)" title="Centauri (Babylon 5)">Centauri</a> is followed from its beginnings as a minor territorial dispute amplified by historical animosity, through to its end, in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> are employed to subjugate and enslave an entire planet. The war is an attempt to portray a more sobering kind of conflict than usually seen on science fiction television. Informed by the events of the first <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring#Invasion" title="Prague Spring">invasion of Prague</a>, the intent was to recreate these moments when "the world held its breath" and the emotional core of the conflict was the disbelief that the situation could have occurred at all, and the desperation to find a way to bring it to an end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> By the start of the third season, the opening monologue had changed to say that the hope for peace had "failed" and the Babylon 5 station had become the "last, best hope for victory", indicating that while peace is a laudable accomplishment, it can also mean a capitulation to an enemy intent on committing horrendous acts, and that "peace is a byproduct of victory against those who do not want peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Shadow_War" title="Shadow War">Shadow War</a> also features prominently in the show, during which an advanced alien species attempts to sow the seeds of conflict in order to promote technological and cultural advancement. The gradual discovery of the scheme and the rebellion against it, serve as the backdrop to the first three seasons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> but also as a metaphor for the war within ourselves. The concurrent limiting of civil liberties and Earth's descent into a dictatorship are "shadow wars" of their own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-home_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-home-34">[34]</a></sup> In ending the Shadow War before the conclusion of the series, the show was able to more fully explore its aftermath, and it is this "war at home" which forms the bulk of the remaining two seasons. The struggle for independence between <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> and Earth culminates with a civil war between the human colonies (led by the Babylon 5 station) and the home planet. Choosing Mars as both the spark for the civil war, and the staging ground for its dramatic conclusion, enabled the viewer to understand the conflict more fully than had it involved an anonymous colony orbiting a distant star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mars_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-mars-16">[16]</a></sup> The conflict, and the reasons behind it, were informed by Nazism, McCarthyism and the breakup of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commie_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-commie-27">[27]</a></sup> and the unraveling of the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balkan" title="Balkan">Balkan</a> country also served as partial inspiration for another civil war, which involved the alien Minbari.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The post-war landscape has its roots in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">Reconstruction</a>. The attempt to resolve the <a href="/wiki/Issues_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Issues of the American Civil War">issues of the American Civil War</a> after the conflict had ended, and this struggle for survival in a changed world was also informed by works such as <i><a href="/wiki/Alas,_Babylon" title="Alas, Babylon">Alas, Babylon</a></i>, a novel dealing with the after-effects of a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">nuclear war</a> on a small American town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The show expresses that the end of these wars is not an end to war itself. Events shown hundreds of years into the show's future tell of wars which will once again bring the human race to the edge of annihilation, demonstrating that mankind will not change, and the best that can be hoped for after it falls is that it climbs a little higher each time, until it can one day "take [its] place among the stars, teaching those who follow."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:45em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>If you look at the long history of human society, religion – whether you describe that as organized, disorganized, or the various degrees of accepted superstition – has always been present. And it will be present 200 years from now... To totally ignore that part of the human equation would be as false and wrong-headed as ignoring the fact that people get mad, or passionate, or strive for better lives.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—J. Michael Straczynski, , 1993<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion1_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-39">[39]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Many of Earth's contemporary religions are shown to still exist, with the main human characters often having religious convictions. Among those specifically identified are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a>), <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and the fictional <a href="/wiki/Foundationism" title="Foundationism">Foundationism</a> (which developed after first contact with alien races).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Alien beliefs in the show range from the <a href="/wiki/Centauri_(Babylon_5)" title="Centauri (Babylon 5)">Centauri</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Bacchanalian</a>-influenced religions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion1_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-39">[39]</a></sup> of which there are up to seventy different denominations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> to the more <a href="/wiki/Pantheism" title="Pantheism">pantheistic</a> as with the <a href="/wiki/Narn" title="Narn">Narn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minbari" title="Minbari">Minbari</a> religions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In the show's third season, a community of <a href="/wiki/Cistercians" title="Cistercians">Cistercian monks</a> takes up residence on the Babylon 5 station, in order to learn what other races call God,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and to come to a better understanding of the different religions through study at close quarters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>References to both human and alien religion is often subtle and brief, but can also form the main theme of an episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The first season episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Parliament_of_Dreams" title="The Parliament of Dreams">The Parliament of Dreams</a>" is a conventional "showcase" for religion, in which each species on the Babylon 5 station has an opportunity to demonstrate its beliefs (humanity's are presented as being numerous and varied),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion1_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-39">[39]</a></sup> while "<a href="/wiki/Passing_Through_Gethsemane" title="Passing Through Gethsemane">Passing Through Gethsemane</a>" focuses on a specific position of Roman Catholic beliefs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> as well as concepts of justice, vengeance, and biblical forgiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Other treatments have been more contentious, such as the <a href="/wiki/David_Gerrold" title="David Gerrold">David Gerrold</a>-scripted "<a href="/wiki/Believers_(Babylon_5)" title="Believers (Babylon 5)">Believers</a>", in which alien parents would rather see their son die than undergo a life-saving operation because their religious beliefs forbid it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion1_39-3"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-39">[39]</a></sup> When religion is an integral part of an episode, various characters express differing view points. Such as in "<a href="/wiki/Soul_Hunter_(Babylon_5)" title="Soul Hunter (Babylon 5)">Soul Hunter</a>", where the concept of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)">immortal soul</a> is touched upon, and whether after death it is destroyed, reincarnated, or simply does not exist. The character arguing the latter, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Franklin_(Babylon_5)" title="Stephen Franklin (Babylon 5)">Doctor Stephen Franklin</a>, often appears in the more spiritual storylines as his scientific rationality is used to create dramatic conflict. Undercurrents of religions such as Buddhism have been viewed by some in various episode scripts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and while identifying himself as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">atheist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religion1_39-4"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-39">[39]</a></sup> Straczynski believes that passages of dialog can take on distinct meanings to viewers of differing faiths, and that the show ultimately expresses ideas which cross religious boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Addiction">Addiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babylon_5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Addiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Substance abuse and its impact on human personalities also plays a significant role in the <i>Babylon 5</i> storyline. The station's security chief, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Garibaldi" title="Michael Garibaldi">Michael Garibaldi</a>, is a textbook relapsing-remitting alcoholic of the <a href="/wiki/Binge_drinking" title="Binge drinking">binge drinking</a> type; he practices complete <a href="/wiki/Abstinence" title="Abstinence">abstinence</a> from alcohol throughout most of the series (with <a href="/wiki/Survivors_(Babylon_5)" title="Survivors (Babylon 5)">one notable exception</a>) until the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Rising_(Babylon_5)" title="Phoenix Rising (Babylon 5)">middle of season five</a>. He only recovers physically and socially and breaks the cycle at the end of the season. His eventual replacement as Chief of Security, <a href="/wiki/Zack_Allan" title="Zack Allan">Zack Allan</a>, was given a second chance by Garibaldi after overcoming his own addiction to an unspecified drug. Dr. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Franklin_(Babylon_5)" title="Stephen Franklin (Babylon 5)">Stephen Franklin</a> develops an (initially unrecognized) addiction to injectable <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulant</a> drugs while trying to cope with the chronic stress and work overload in Medlab, and wanders off to the homeless and deprived in Brown Sector, where he suffers through a severe <a href="/wiki/Drug_withdrawal" title="Drug withdrawal">withdrawal</a> syndrome. Executive Officer <a href="/wiki/Susan_Ivanova" title="Susan Ivanova">Susan Ivanova</a> mentions that her father became an alcoholic after her mother had committed suicide after having been drugged by the authorities over a number of years. Captain <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Lochley" title="Elizabeth Lochley">Elizabeth Lochley</a> tells Garibaldi that her father was an alcoholic and that she is a recovering alcoholic herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
